--- Commit Message ---
LU-14958 kernel: use rhashtable for revoke records in jbd2

resizable hashtable should improve journal replay time when
the latter has got million of revoke records. notice that
rhashtable is used during replay only as removal with list_del()
is less expensive and it's used a lot during regular processing.

before:
1048576 records - 95 seconds
2097152 records - 580 seconds

after:
1048576 records - 2 seconds
2097152 records - 3 seconds
4194304 records - 7 seconds

Signed-off-by: Alex Zhuravlev <bzzz@whamcloud.com>

Patch Set 2:

for a reason rhashtable_walk_next() misses the records. before the walk I save nelems, in the loop I count all returned records and after the loop I check nelems again:

!! dm-0-8 lost recs in n 00000000787d9abb: was 27, now 5, count 22

i..e. it's not new records, it's missed ones?

> Is this the for all the walks ?
no, not every time. it looks like removal affects a current position and some records get skipped. I tried to check usecases in the kernel, but haven't found one with walk+remove. there is free_and_destroy, but actually I don't want to destroy hashtable, just drop all the records.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2022-03-21 02:47:01.000000000) ---
Patch Set 18: Code-Review+1

My only concern is that without this patch jbd2_journal_set_revoke() can NEVER fail.  There is code to handle failure but it isn't being tested.
With the patch it CAN fail because rhashtable insertion can fail transiently.
So I'd rather a retry loop, but I don't think that is enough to block the patch as failure is extremely unlikely.
